#  [](/thread/23592-pabloski-system)pabloski System 

  * 

  * [#1](/thread/23592-pabloski-system "Post Permalink")

  * First Post: Apr 8, 2007 10:23am  Apr 8, 2007 10:23am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar15327_5.gif) pabloski](pabloski)

  * | Joined Aug 2006  | Status: Trader | [356 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=15327) | Online Now 

I have been studying the fascinating world of FOREX for more than two years and ForexFactory was one of the first places were I found valuable help and information. I usually spend all of my time in this forum reading and learning, so I think now is the time to share.  
I have created and tested many many systems during all this months and finally there is one it seems to generate regular profits for me. I have only tested it on GBP/JPY. I have fund that H4 is the best timeframe to spot firm trends and reasonably early. We know that trends in GBP/JPY are strong and prolonged, but it's not that easy to recognize its beginnings and the right time to exit. I'm sure this system should work with other pairs with the right adjustments if needed, as each pair has its own personality.  
TPs and SLs for this system are “dynamic”, as I called them, because they change according to the indicators used. You will understand what I mean once you read the logics. At first it may look a bit complex, but soon you will realize it's easy to follow and understand. Of course, charts with examples will finally give you the full picture.  
  
Ok, let's start. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f601.png?v=15.1)  
  
This system uses two visible indicators: ATR Channels and StepChoppyBars v1.1, which needs to work properly StepMA v7 and StepRSI v5.2 indicators.  
StepChoppyBars is a great indicator created by Igorad from Forex-TSD.com forum. Legend for StepChoppyBars indicator is the following:  
Blue: Strong UpTrend.  
DodgerBlue: Retrace UpTrend  
LightBlue: Choppy UpTrend  
Aqua: Be ready to change UpTrend  
Red: Strong DownTrend  
Tomato: Retrace DownTrend  
Orange: Choppy DownTrend  
Yellow: Be ready to change DownTrend  
  
Buy & Close-Buy Logics  
Buy three equal positions when a candle closes between Lime ATR Centre Line and Aqua ATR Line, Step Choppy Bars candle is blue and previous Step Choppy Bar candle is Blue or Yellow. SL for the three opened positions is a candle closing below Yellow ATR line.  
TP for the first position is a candle closing above Aqua ATR line. Once this TP is reached, the SL of the two remaining open positions will be moved to breakeven. TP for the second position is a candle closing above DodgerBlue ATR line. Once this TP is reached, the SL of the remaining open position will be a candle close below Aqua ATR line. If trend continues and price “touches” Blue ATR line, SL of this last position will be now a candle closing below DodgerBlue ATR line. This last position will remain opened till SL is triggered or a candle is painted Aqua.  
Note: In the case a candle is painted Red, Tomato, Orange or Yellow during any time of the process, all positions should be closed.  
  
Sell & Close-Sell Logics  
Sell three equal positions when a candle closes between ATR Lime centre line and ATR Yellow line, Step Choppy Bars candle is red and previous Step Choppy Bar candle is Red or Aqua. Initial SL for the three opened positions is a candle closing above Aqua ATR line.  
TP for the first position is a candle closing below Yellow ATR line. Once this TP is reached, the SL of the two remaining open positions will be moved to breakeven. TP for the second position is when a candle closing below Orange ATR line. Once this TP is reached, the SL of the remaining open position will be a candle closing above Yellow ATR line. If trend continues and price “touches” Red ATR line, SL of the last opened position will be now a candle closing above Orange ATR line. This last position will remain opened till SL is triggered or a candle is painted Yellow.  
Note: In the case a candle is painted Blue, DodgerBlue, LightBlue or Aqua during any time of the process, all positions should be closed.  
  
Note: If we see a sell opportunity but the candle is closing between Yellow and Orange lines (instead between Lime and Yellow lines), **very close to yellow line** , you may:  
\- Open three positions, apply the TPs and SLs for the 2nd and 3rd positions as usual and use the same TPs and SLs than the 2nd position for the 1st position.  
\- Open two positions, ignoring the 1st one and applying TPs and SLs for the 2nd and 3rd positions as usual.  
The same logic applies to a buy opportunity, but doesn't happen frequently.  
  
When taking a position, always wait for the candle to close. A possible variation would be opening only one position and moving the SLs accordingly.  
  
What I like about this system is that it generally gives accurate signals and if not, will tell you to exit early avoiding big losses. Also, it's very likely that for not so prolonged trends at least the first TP will be reached, so you will generally exit happy with profits. The system requires attention but not so much, it's enough to take a look at the chart every 4 hours to see how the candle is closing.   
  
Of course, always test every system before risking real money. This is open to modifications and improvements, fell free to comment! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)  
  
pabloski

Short 1.31 08:00 according to rules entry must between lime and yellow lines. This one is below yellow line, so no entry.  
Short 2.5 04:00 237.31t/p 2.5 08:00 236.27 (below yellow line) profit +104-9spread +95 on one pos the rest break even  
long 2.7 08:00 237.46 t/p 2.8 8:00 238.46 profit 100-9=91  
short 2.9 08:00 236.59 s/l 2.11 20:00 238.36 (hit aqua line) loss (-177-9)*3=-558 hey that's a lot  
short 2.12 12:00 237.41 t/p 2.13 12:00 235.67 profit 174-9=165 the rest b/e  
short 2.15 04:00 235.81 t/p 2.15 12:00 profit-1 235.05 74-9=85  
profit-2 2.15 16:00 233.45 240-9=231  
looks like last pos is the same profit 231, since it touched red atr line  
  
So total is 349 in this bad period

> [Quoting irusoh](/thread/post/265976#post265976 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Short 1.31 08:00 according to rules entry must between lime and yellow lines. This one is below yellow line, so no entry.  
>  Short 2.5 04:00 237.31t/p 2.5 08:00 236.27 (below yellow line) profit +104-9spread +95 on one pos the rest break even  
>  long 2.7 08:00 237.46 t/p 2.8 8:00 238.46 profit 100-9=91

Hi Irusoh, thank you for you input. Im afraid there is one little correction to make. Everything is ok in you count except this short position:  
  

> Quote
> 
> Disliked
> 
> short 2.9 08:00 236.59 s/l 2.11 20:00 238.36 (hit aqua line) loss (-177-9)*3=-558

First, you should go short at 12:00, because at 8:00 previous candle is not painted red or aqua. Second, the position never reached SL because a candle never closes above Aqua Line. If you read the logics, SL is a candle closing above Aqua Line (not touching aqua line).  
  
According to my count, results for that position are:  
  
Sell @ 236.56 - 12:00  
First TP @ 235.76  
SL (breakeven) reached @ 236.53 for 2nd and 3rd position.  
Total Pips: 69  
  
Please see chart attached. 

Attached Image

  * Apr 9, 2007 3:43am  Apr 9, 2007 3:43am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar15327_5.gif) pabloski](pabloski)

  * | Joined Aug 2006  | Status: Trader | [356 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=15327) | Online Now 

> [Quoting Vitaliy](/thread/post/266068#post266068 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> This is a great system ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1) thnx to those people who could defend it from my criticizing ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1) but to make three orders and not to go down on those parts that i pointed out on the charts you need pretty big balance to cover these swings ....  
>    
>  100 pip jump back x 3 = 300 , so its pretty significant number ...
> 
> Ignored

True, but I think that if you open three positions, you should divide your usual lot size by 3. For example, if you usually open 0.1 lot, then open three position of 3 microlots. If you usually open 1 lot, then open three positions of 0.3 lots, etc. This is how you can manage your risk.  
As I said in the 1st post, you may also open only one position and let it ride moving only SLs (or choosing the TP you wish).  
Everthing can be adapted to fit your needs.

>  short 2.15 04:00 235.81 t/p 2.15 12:00 profit-1 235.05 74-9=85  
>  profit-2 2.15 16:00 233.45 240-9=231  
>  looks like last pos is the same profit 231, since it touched red atr line  
>    
>  So total is 349 in this bad period
> 
> Ignored

  * [#46](/thread/post/266349#post266349 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 9, 2007 11:48am  Apr 9, 2007 11:48am 

  * [ Blackeagle](blackeagle)

  * Joined Aug 2005 | Status: Trader | [1,188 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=3166)

If you divide your usual lot size by 3 to manage risk, this means you are cutting your reward as well which keeps your risk/reward ratio the same.  
  
The logic behind your strategy is consistent, but SL will be a problem if all three positions are stopped before hitting the first TP. My Alpari platform shows a Long entry 03/29 @ 231.52 with three lots. At that moment, yellow ATR line is @ 229.7991. If the price closes below this level, let's say 229.78, we will be stopped out with the minimum loss of -174 pips x 3 = -522 pips.   
  
If the position is opened towards Aqua ATR line (for longs) and stopped out towards Orange ATR line due to using the closing price only, there is always the risk of higher SL amounts. As a result, you'll need high winning ratio to overcome this SL issue as well as long and strong trending prices to exit the third lot at a considerable profit to improve overall risk/reward ratio of this system.  
  
Thanks for sharing your system.  
  
  

> [Quoting pabloski](/thread/post/266073#post266073 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> True, but I think that if you open three positions, you should divide your usual lot size by 3. For example, if you usually open 0.1 lot, then open three position of 3 microlots. If you usually open 1 lot, then open three positions of 0.3 lots, etc. This is how you can manage your risk.  
>  As I said in the 1st post, you may also open only one position and let it ride moving only SLs (or choosing the TP you wish).  
>  Everthing can be adapted to fit your needs.
> 
> Ignored

  * [#52](/thread/post/266858#post266858 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 10, 2007 3:46am  Apr 10, 2007 3:46am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar15327_5.gif) pabloski](pabloski)

  * | Joined Aug 2006  | Status: Trader | [356 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=15327) | Online Now 

> [Quoting Blackeagle](/thread/post/266349#post266349 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> If you divide your usual lot size by 3 to manage risk, this means you are cutting your reward as well which keeps your risk/reward ratio the same.  
>    
>  The logic behind your strategy is consistent, but SL will be a problem if all three positions are stopped before hitting the first TP. My Alpari platform shows a Long entry 03/29 @ 231.52 with three lots. At that moment, yellow ATR line is @ 229.7991. If the price closes below this level, let's say 229.78, we will be stopped out with the minimum loss of -174 pips x 3 = -522 pips.   
>    
>  If the position is opened towards Aqua ATR line (for longs) and stopped out towards Orange ATR line due to using the closing price only, there is always the risk of higher SL amounts. As a result, you'll need high winning ratio to overcome this SL issue as well as long and strong trending prices to exit the third lot at a considerable profit to improve overall risk/reward ratio of this system.  
>    
>  Thanks for sharing your system.
> 
> Ignored

I understand your point. However, if you divide you lot size by 3, its not necessary to multiply negative pips by 3. If you sum up total pips lost for the three positions, you should at the same time consider that those positions are 1/3 of your original lot size each. So, you are loosing almost the same if you open 1 lot than if you open three positions of 0.3 lot each.  
Those ugly -522 pips for the three positions are in fact -174 pips for your regular lot size.  
  
The reason I decide to open three positions becomes obvious when you test and see the system working. A high percentage of the positions you enter reaches 1st TP. At that point you are free of any possible loss. But also at that point sometimes the trend continues and sometimes not. You cannot be sure about what will happen, so you have two remaining positions with SL at breakeven that have a great potential to close with high earnings (or at cero in the worst case).  
  
Thank you for your contribution! 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

#  [](/thread/23592-pabloski-system)pabloski System 

  * 

  * [#61](/thread/post/267103#post267103 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 10, 2007 9:42am  Apr 10, 2007 9:42am 

  * [ Blackeagle](blackeagle)

  * Joined Aug 2005 | Status: Trader | [1,188 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=3166)

That's why I said your risk reward ratio will not change. You can have -522 pips loss, but your profits will be high too. If you open three positions of 0.3 lot each, you will have -174 pips loss but your profit in total will be reduced proportionally compared to trading standard lots.  
  
And I agree with you to trade this system with multiple lots, because it provides better risk management.  
  
  

> [Quoting pabloski](/thread/post/266858#post266858 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I understand your point. However, if you divide you lot size by 3, its not necessary to multiply negative pips by 3. If you sum up total pips lost for the three positions, you should at the same time consider that those positions are 1/3 of your original lot size each. So, you are loosing almost the same if you open 1 lot than if you open three positions of 0.3 lot each.  
>  Those ugly -522 pips for the three positions are in fact -174 pips for your regular lot size.  
>    
>  The reason I decide to open three positions becomes obvious when you test and see the system working. A high percentage of the positions you enter reaches 1st TP. At that point you are free of any possible loss. But also at that point sometimes the trend continues and sometimes not. You cannot be sure about what will happen, so you have two remaining positions with SL at breakeven that have a great potential to close with high earnings (or at cero in the worst case).  
>    
>  Thank you for your contribution!
> 
> Ignored

> [Quoting Blackeagle](/thread/post/267152#post267152 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I am attaching my GBPJPY chart on Alpari server and please compare it with the one on your post #56. As you will see, there are differences. I am not sure if the one on post#56 is from Alpari. It looks it is from Metaquotes Corp. which may have different data feed and therefore different bars.  
>  After I have read your first post, I have found the original thread on tsd forum and there are a couple people there complaining about different charts on different mt4 platforms. I am using Alpari and will stick to it to follow your system.  
>  A few people on tsd forum also complained about repainting of the bars, I have been watching the indicator since yesterday and I haven't seen such a repainting yet.
> 
> Ignored

Yes, I see some colour differences between Alpari chart and Metaquotes chart, but it's not indicators fault. These variations are because of the differences between Alpari data and Metaquotes data. Just compare candles opens, closes, highs and lows and you'll notice considerable disparities.   
  
Just as an example. See (in 4H chart) candle **28.03.2007 4:00  
  
** For Alpari data:  
Open: 230.64  
High: 230.89  
Low: 229.89  
Close: 230.29  
  
For Metaquotes data:  
Open: 231.65  
High: 231.69  
Low: 230.03  
Close: 230.17  
  
StepChoppyBars seems to be very sensitive to price quotation, so I think this should be the reason.  
  
Regarding bars repainting, that seems to happen sometimes on shorter timeframes like M1 and M5. For longer timeframes like H1, H4, D1 I haven't seen bars repainting during all this time.

> 
> Disliked
> 
> From the rules:  
>    
>  Hi Pabloski,   
>  I wanted to clarify something.   
>  When opening new trade, it opens at the open of the new bar and 2 previous bars are blue or first is blue and second is yellow.   
>    
>  Is that correct.?  
>    
>  First I got the impression that as soon as last bar was blue you can open.  
>  I am making backtest EA for this and wanted to clarify.
> 
> Ignored

Hi Irusoh,  
  
The rule to buy is that the bar for the candle that has just closed is painted blue, and the previous bar is blue or yellow. To sell, the bar for the candle that has just closed is painted red, and the previous bar is red or aqua. You must always wait for the candle to close. The last candle that is still opened is not considered.  
  
Hope it helps! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44d.png?v=15.1)

Attached Image

![](/attachment/image/28383?d=1176249190)

If you read the logics, candle must close between lime and aqua lines. You may also buy if a candle closes between aqua and dodgerblue lines but VERY close to aqua line (when I say VERY close, I mean candle closing no more than 10 pips away from aqua line).  
  
So, answering your question, you can consider the previous candle as a signal to buy as its closing very close to aqua line. I didnt see this ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f61c.png?v=15.1):, thank you!  
  
Im in with 3 positions. To know what is my 1st TP read the logics.  
  
Best wishes!

Hi pabloski,  
  
You said SL for the three opened LONG positions is a candle closing below Yellow ATR line. And you also said we should open three SHORT positions when a candle closes between ATR Lime centre line and ATR Yellow line.  
  
Regarding recent LONG position form 234.85, let's say we have a close between centre lime line and yellow line with a red candle and previous candle is red or aqua. In this case, SL for the long position will be between centre lime line and yellow line since we are going to close our long position and open short.  
  
Therefore, in practice, can we say SL is not ALWAYS below yellow line (for longs) or above aqua line (for shorts) depending on the colours of StepChoppy candles?

> Quote
> 
> Disliked
> 
> "You said SL for the three opened LONG positions is a candle closing below Yellow ATR line. And you also said we should open three SHORT positions when a candle closes between ATR Lime centre line and ATR Yellow line."

This is right.  
  

> Quote
> 
> Disliked
> 
> "Regarding recent LONG position form 234.85, let's say we have a close between centre lime line and yellow line with a red candle and previous candle is red or aqua. In this case, SL for the long position will be between centre lime line and yellow line since we are going to close our long position and open short.  
>  Therefore, in practice, can we say SL is not ALWAYS below yellow line (for longs) or above aqua line (for shorts) depending on the colours of StepChoppy candles?"

  
This is right. However, I dont consider this as a SL for the long position. If you read the logics: **"In the case a candle is painted Red, Tomato, Orange or Yellow during any time of the process, all positions should be closed."** So long positions are closed because of what previous rule says, not because SL was reached.

  * [#98](/thread/post/269692#post269692 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 12, 2007 10:56am  Apr 12, 2007 10:56am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar17832_4.gif) TeamAphid](teamaphid)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: Team Work!!!! | [302 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=17832)

Thanks Pabloski for sharing your strategy.   
  
We have finished testing GBPJPY with your rules on post #1. From Jan 06 to April 07, total profit is 9,285 pips. # of total trades is 57 with 45 wins and 12 losses giving 78.9% win ratio (If you look at monthly figures, the one we prefer to evaluate systems, there are 4 months with losses out of 15 which gives us 73.3% winning ratio). Max loss with 3 lots is -720 pips (-240 pips per lot) and losses are generally not less than 100 pips per lot. The results is promising for a trend following strategy, but there are a few issues we'd like to discuss.   
  
First of all, 7631 pips of total profits (82.2%) are coming from 4 months (Feb & Apr 06, Feb & Mar 07) and 4931 pips (53.1%) are coming from last 2 months which had exceptionally strong moves, both up and down, on GBPJPY. Secondly, a consistent uptrend/downtrend is not enough to get a good result from any trade, the move should be very strong, because there are many trades ended at BE (second and third lots) (though it is good in a sense of riding a risk-free trade) although they caught the move in early stages. Therefore, our recommendations would be to modify SL strategy and maybe the rule for exiting the 3rd lot to increase the profit potential. Because, sometimes, due to a strong move, price hit the last ATR line and then consolidates. During this consolidation period, ATR lines keep moving in trade direction but the bar is closed in SL area (above orange line or below dodger blue line) due to this horizontal move. So, we noticed during the backtests that some trades exited the third lot very early. Another recommendation would be to trade 4 lots instead of 3 and trailing the 4th lot similar to the 3rd lot (after modifying the 3rd lot exit). Drawdown can be seen a bit too much (-720 pips) by many others, but we believe it is not for this pair and a trend following strategy, though can be reduced by modifying SL rules (we are going to work on this as TeamAphid).  
  
Anyway, our recommendation in overall is to modify some of the SL and exit rules (these should be backtested properly before amending the original rules)in order to have much more consistent results and not depend on a few months of very strong moves. We believe this method is profitable in the long run if applied with discipline, especially on GBPJPY as it is the most trending pair.  
  
ps. We did not put exit dates and times on backtest spreadsheet to speed up testing process. You can find them by using prices. We used Alpari server and historical data in our tests.   
  
Regards,  
TeamAphid

These are my counts for the Jan, Feb and March 2006. Using logics exactly as stated including the option:  
Buy if a candle closes between aqua and dodgerblue lines but VERY close to aqua line (no more than 10 pips away from aqua line). Sell if a candle closes between yellow and orange lines but VERY close to yellow line (no more than 10 pips away from yellow line).  
Results include spread. In the charts you can see "StepChoppy" indicator which exactly the same as "stepChoppyBars" but shows bars colours in a separate window.  
  
Buy 03.01 20:00 @ 202.98  
1st TP @ 204.16  
2nd & 3rd SL reached @ breakeven  
+109 pips  
  
Sell 06.01 16:00 @ 202.39  
1st TP @ 201.53  
2nd & 3rd SL reached @ breakeven  
+77 pips  
  
Sell 12.01 8:00 @ 201.09 (opening 2 positions, closing between yellow and orange line).  
Close all positions @ 202.32 with blue bar.  
-264 pips  
  
Buy 13.01 8:00 @ 202.32  
1st TP @ 203.37  
2nd & 3rd SL reached @ breakeven  
+96 pips  
  
Sell 19.01 8:00 @ 202.28  
Close all positions @ 203.33 with blue bar.  
-342 pips  
  
Buy 20.01 16:00 @ 203.93 (opening two positions, opening between aqua and doger blue line).  
2nd TP @ 206.75  
3rd TP 207.67  
+638 pips

> [Quoting TeamAphid](/thread/post/269692#post269692 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Thanks Pabloski for sharing your strategy.   
>    
>  We have finished testing GBPJPY with your rules on post #1. From Jan 06 to April 07, total profit is 9,285 pips. # of total trades is 57 with 45 wins and 12 losses giving 78.9% win ratio (If you look at monthly figures, the one we prefer to evaluate systems, there are 4 months with losses out of 15 which gives us 73.3% winning ratio). Max loss with 3 lots is -720 pips (-240 pips per lot) and losses are generally not less than 100 pips per lot. The results is promising for a trend following strategy, but there are a few issues we'd like to discuss.   
>    
>  First of all, 7631 pips of total profits (82.2%) are coming from 4 months (Feb & Apr 06, Feb & Mar 07) and 4931 pips (53.1%) are coming from last 2 months which had exceptionally strong moves, both up and down, on GBPJPY. Secondly, a consistent uptrend/downtrend is not enough to get a good result from any trade, the move should be very strong, because there are many trades ended at BE (second and third lots) (though it is good in a sense of riding a risk-free trade) although they caught the move in early stages. Therefore, our recommendations would be to modify SL strategy and maybe the rule for exiting the 3rd lot to increase the profit potential. Because, sometimes, due to a strong move, price hit the last ATR line and then consolidates. During this consolidation period, ATR lines keep moving in trade direction but the bar is closed in SL area (above orange line or below dodger blue line) due to this horizontal move. So, we noticed during the backtests that some trades exited the third lot very early. Another recommendation would be to trade 4 lots instead of 3 and trailing the 4th lot similar to the 3rd lot (after modifying the 3rd lot exit). Drawdown can be seen a bit too much (-720 pips) by many others, but we believe it is not for this pair and a trend following strategy, though can be reduced by modifying SL rules (we are going to work on this as TeamAphid).  
>    
>  Anyway, our recommendation in overall is to modify some of the SL and exit rules (these should be backtested properly before amending the original rules)in order to have much more consistent results and not depend on a few months of very strong moves. We believe this method is profitable in the long run if applied with discipline, especially on GBPJPY as it is the most trending pair.  
>    
>  ps. We did not put exit dates and times on backtest spreadsheet to speed up testing process. You can find them by using prices. We used Alpari server and historical data in our tests.   
>    
>  Regards,  
>  TeamAphid
> 
> Ignored

>  Buy if a candle closes between aqua and dodgerblue lines but VERY close to aqua line (no more than 10 pips away from aqua line). Sell if a candle closes between yellow and orange lines but VERY close to yellow line (no more than 10 pips away from yellow line).

  * [#115](/thread/post/271809#post271809 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 14, 2007 2:24am  Apr 14, 2007 2:24am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar13263_4.gif) irusoh](irusoh)

  * | Joined Jul 2006  | Status: Stupid MQL Tricks Master | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=13263)

To answer Team Aphid question I use alpari data that I took from alpari UK databank. I converted M1 data into all other timeframes for which I use my own script to synchronize alpari data in all timeframes. I ran it on Velocity Trader server, which essentially makes no difference except for spread may vary by dealer.  
  
One serious mistake that may happen with backtesting is unsynhronized data across different timeframes. That is M1 data does not correspond to H4 data, for example loading M1 data from alpari but leaving H4 data that was in history before. The important thing is not which server is running the data but the data be completely synchornized from M1.  
So I loaded synchronized M1 thru D1 data for 2006 into history.  
The second important thing when backtesting is to use MT visual tester even for manual backtesting. Quite often indicators give signals differently in real time rather than just looking back at historical chart. Thus certain entries that didn't take place in historical chart may happen in real time since signal was given and then erased later on recalculation.  
I used EA that picked up signals as they were presented at the time of evaluation.  
  
Of course choppybars may look different on different charts too due to various timeshifts with different dealers but then again good system can't depend on how signal is generated based on time shift and should on average make money regardless.  
  
The only difference in my expert was that it chose to exit instantly when bar changed from blue colors to red colors on a buy and vice versa. It seemed sometimes it gave a better exit point than just waiting for s/l to be hit. But it doesn't seem to happen very often.  
  
I am waiting anxiously for improvement suggetstions from Pabloski and/or Team Aphid to incorporate into the system.

That trade (04/12 08:00 bar LONG) is the main difference between our April results. Since it is within 10 pips range of green line, as explained in the strategy, we chose to take 3 positions here which gave us +497 pips. These kind of situations will vary the results as taking the trade is discretionary depending on your risk appetite.  
  
We compared your charts (as much as we can see) with our and they are almost identical. We are, as a team, doing all our backtests ONLY manually.

Hi,  
I did a research, and the result varies, the most confident entry level was after a candles yellow and blue, you shoul enter after the signal was given,(yellow folowed by a blue candle). I just did the research in the GBP/USD 15M and 30M. I found better results in 15M charts. I looked into 4H charts, but the result varies and not so good, and we have to set a higher S/L. I dont like my short stack of money floating with those monster out there.Every pair has is own conditions, I will posted the results as long I finished with the others. So, you should find your comfort zone and investing strategies. I like short entries, and avoid get hit by markets news and market corrections. I enter strong trying to profit in the short run. Eleven signals in march and 9 went perfect, 40, 27, 32, 52, 21,20,39, 105, 142, I will close 80% with 20 pips and the other 20 i let it run moving my S/L to make 10 pips in the other 20%. Next target will be 40 where I will close the other 15%, let it run the other 5% and moving the S/L to 20 pips gain, Which is my confort winning zone. I usually enter with 20 standart lots or 200 usd every pips it moves. I'm happy making $20,000 a month. The other two trades that went wrong were -26 and -25, but i always put 20 pips S/L. we could chance to avoid those losses, for the trade lasted longer than usual, almost 6 and 8 hrs to lose our money. I will recommend if after 2 hours it hasn't move as expected, we should close our position. If doing it, we should profit from those losses18 and 17 pips respectively, Which it makes it 11 out 11 trades. 100% perfect trades. Anyway, let it run after closing at 20 pips profit, we could easily upset the losses. Becarful with MT4 signals, it gives me completely different signals between accounts, I had 2 accounts and a demo, and my partner has another 2 accounts, one of my account give me different signals, for it workd with another server, so beware you do not received wrong signals. Finally, tested with small lots until you gain confidence and get familiar withy the indicator.   
  
Up- trends signal:  
Yellow- blue: strong signal...  
blue-blue:weak signal...i get 60% result  
  
down trends:  
acqua-red: strong signal. 55% result  
red-red:weak signal. 41% results  
  
check before trade, and good luck!!!!  
I hope that can be useful information!!!!!  
  
  
check fridays signals:  
down trend was an excellent signal.entry at 1.9825 it went down to 1,9781..  
investing 10 standard lots or 100usd per 1 pips it moves...  
first close at 20 pips or 1.9801...profit $1600 move S/L to 1.9835  
second close at 40 pips 1.9781..15% profit $600 move S/L to 1.9825  
Let it run the other 5%, which retraces to 1.9801..profit $100  
total profit: $2300  
  
and then after the up-trend yellow-blue:  
enter 1.9849 close 80% at 1.9869 profit $1600 move S/L to 1.9859  
second close at 1.9889, but it retraced to 1.9856, so we close the other 20% profit $200  
total profit:$1800...  
  
not bad for a 4hr trade... total profit $4100....  
Always use your take a profit manager so you avoid fast market movements and no need to set your S/L and take a profit manually or do any calcalutions, and always hide your S/L and take a profit targets from your broker, so they could not see where your S/L is...and activate your expert advisors once you close the 80% you dont need to stay in front of the computer all day....  
Once again Good Luck!!!!

ATR Lines will only confirm the volatility ahead..as the ATR widened the volatility is low....when they are narrowing something big is coming...check today before the big jump....only a difference of 50 pips between the two extremes..after the economic releases more than 200 pips...if you go backwards it happens in most of the cases..todays weak uptrend signal(blue-blue)...which is 60% effective...using it properly almost 67%....gaves the entry point GBP/USD at 1.9922, before the news release it was already at 1.9940...i will played safe at economic releases with a S/L...but even after the economic release it gaves us again the weak up trend signal at 2.0024 and it went up to 2.0073, but i will only go for 20 pips closing 80% of my position...and then so on....another 15% at 40 pips and let it run...but with weak signal i will say closed your entire position with 20 pips profit...olnly 13% of the weak signal trend reach 40 pips gain...i will not take that risk...the purpose is open and lock in your profits..more signal will come for sure...that's trading wait for the right time and right moment..always trying to enter the market when we have the advantage...even the bulls with michael jordan lost 12 games in that memorable season...and brazil lost the world cup...no one really knows what's going to happen..otherwise we should not be here trying to figure it out how to beat the market...so keep the calm and do not fustrate when we have 4 or 5 bad trades in a row...try to equalize all trades..and do not put more weight in some trades than other...avoid surprises...all trades equals....thanks pablosky...working in GBP/JPY...and I will put close attetion to the ATR movements..to close our positions...Thanks for the feedback..

  * Apr 19, 2007 5:19am  Apr 19, 2007 5:19am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar15327_5.gif) pabloski](pabloski)

  * | Joined Aug 2006  | Status: Trader | [356 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=15327) | Online Now 

Thanks Bluemiami for your inputs. As I told you, Ill test your variation and let you know my results.  
  
Im sorry for my late post, I have been studying and looking many ways to improve this system during these days.  
Finally, after testing A LOT of indicators, I have came across one called "TrendPower" which seems to do an amazing job filtering trades. To test it, I used TeamAphid backtest.  
  
Rules for filtering trades with TrendPower indicator are:  
Buy if TrendPower value is >= 0.14  
Sell if TrendPower value us <= -0.14  
  
Settings for the indicator are:  
ADXPeriod=14  
SMAFast=5  
SMASlow=14  
  
So, what results did I get? From ThemAphid backtest, ALL negative trades except 1 were filtered. That is only 1 losing trade for 15 months. On the other side, it filtered also some positive trades but most of them were trades that resulted in small profit (this is explaned as they were from weaker trends). Many trades were modified as the entry point was triggered some candles after.  
  
Results:  
Total trades=33  
Winning trades=32 (97%)  
Losing trades=1 (3%)  
  
Total pips: +11221  
  
No losing months, all in profit.  
  
Like it? ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f601.png?v=15.1)  
  
I think this can be perfectly adjusted for other trending pairs and other timeframes with excellent results. We just need to adjust the settings and entry levels for TrendPower indicator and also we may change general rules of the system itself.  
  
Check the .xls file and indicator attached.  
  
Best wishes!

  * [#144](/thread/post/276414#post276414 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 19, 2007 10:34am  Apr 19, 2007 10:34am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar13263_4.gif) irusoh](irusoh)

  * | Joined Jul 2006  | Status: Stupid MQL Tricks Master | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=13263)

I've been doing some testing of my own with this system using an Expert Advisor.  
  
I've come to the following results.  
  
1\. It seems best setting for ATR channels indicator is 1.4,2.9,4.0  
2\. When setting s/l after first close, it is better to wait for the bar to close first. If bar closes higher (on buy) set s/l at breakeven, otherwise close trade at once  
3\. Wait for the last unit to close (below/above) green line (on buy/sell) at all times eliminating all complex rules with touching blue line etc.  
4\. My test showed (from 8/2004 to 12/2006) that there were only 4 trades that closed 2nd unit and then went to b/e. So I eliminated 2nd unit close and hold 2 last units as per rule 3.  
  
in my tests after applying these rules results approximately doubled.  
  
This was a test for GBPJPY.

  * [#145](/thread/post/276446#post276446 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 19, 2007 11:27am  Apr 19, 2007 11:27am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar17832_4.gif) TeamAphid](teamaphid)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: Team Work!!!! | [302 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=17832)

After testing GBPJPY, we have decided to test EURJPY and GBPUSD to see if pabloski system is profitable for these pairs as well.  
  
When we finished the first four months of testing EURJPY, we wanted to check the results and see if the stepchoppy indicator was repainting. We saw that most of the entry bar colours went one bar backward (ie. entry at 12:00 bar became an entry at 08:00 bar). Some of the entry bars went backward multiple bars (4/5 bars backward) and some of the entries were missed during the backtests and some of the entries shouldn't have been taken. After years of manual backtesting experience of Team Aphid, we have decided that this cannot be a mistake by us, and the conclusion was the indicator is repainting. We wanted to test GBPUSD as well to make sure of this situation and the indicator has repainted itself on this pair as well.  
  
Now, the strange thing is that we have been keeping records of every bar colour of GBPJPY since April 9th and we check our backtest results posted on this thread twice everyday to see if the indicator repaints, and the colours are still 100% matching. So, the indicator repaints itself on EURJPY and GBPUSD, but does not repaint on GBPJPY. That's pretty weird, we think.  
  
Another observation is that we used same broker, same server, same platform and same open/high/low/close prices, everything was the same bar by bar on two different computers, but the colours of the bars were different.  
  
Our conclusion on this issue is that Stepchoppy indicator is not stable, but somehow it still did not repaint on GBPJPY and it is still stable on this pair only. We keep watching it on GBPJPY and if it repaints, we'll inform you asap.  
  
ps. we only use 4hr time frame, not shorter ones.

I think it has to be happenstance that the GBP/JPY was not observed repainting.   
  
The programing allows a bar to change color after close and I don't see how a particular pair could be exempt from that.  
  
I've followed a lot of false leads on systems that looked great on a chart and they turned out to be repainting. This is nothing new.

Hi Guys,  
I have been looking all day at 15M charts, to see if the bars repaints, but so far, it has not repainted. I am just looking for the big markets swings to enter into a position, especially after news trades, so far pablosky's system keeps giving me those profitable signals.  
Today, 4/20 at 4.30am eastern time USA, I did a trade on GBP/JPY retail sales. Before the news, the price opened at 237.93, the bar before was acqua, then went down to 237.46 closing at 237.48 the bar closed red. Strong dowtrend signal was given, so I enter the next one at 237.49 after almost 50 pips down in 30M and 82 pips since the european markets open at 2:00 AM or 2:30 hours. So, it finally went down to 237.18, but I closed my 20 pips profit at 237.21 using my take a profit manager, beacuse it rebounds back so fast that I could not even have a chance to close it manually, and most important the bar did not repaint, at least in my demo account which is the one that gives me the right signal.   
OHHHH...I just look into my demo platform GBP/USD also, and everything worked fine too. it gave the downtrend signal perfectly (aqua-red). I could not trade because I was trading the GBP/USD, but also we could profit 20 pips following the acqua-red strong downtrend signal...  
On the other hand, my live account gaves me different signals, only acqua-acqua-acqua, and completely different colors afterward, but it never gave me the acqua-red and desired entry signal. Right now, I have a weak uptrend signal (blue-blue-blue) in my live account, but my demo platform is giving me(yellow-yellow-orange), so no trade. So, I stick with my demo platform which is working perfectly, and the one fortunely I did the research on. Otherwise, I could not be trading on pabloski's system today. Reasons why I told you to confirm trading signals before entering any trade, and do your personal reasearch.   
I have been watching the only pairs I trade after the sad news of repaint, GBP/USD, GBP/JPY, ERU/JPY, USD/JPY, EUR/USD and at least all day today, it has not repaint after a bar closed(15M CHARTS ONLY). I repeat, I havent seen any repaint. If anyone has seen something different in 15M charts feel free to comment please. I noticed that bars repaint before closing the 15M cycle, but after the bar closed the previous one has not repainted yet, At least in todays personal experiment.   
I just try to follow the market trend, and when everyone is selling at unison , no one is buying, except some no brain like me at times before, then prices drop like crazy, especially in such speculative pair like GBP,JPY that's a market behavior, and I just followed and profit from that behavior. Who control the market, banks!!! Bank's traders have rules to follow, they called trading policy, we, the small fish,do not have any policy, we enter anytime without a boss behind and a set of undefine and undisciplined rules( I included myself, working on improvement). We just loss( in most cases) or win our money, not a job or reputation. So, when they enter the market all bank's traders(who has the biggest volume and price movements influences) follow the same rules, if the economic releases was below expectations, which bank will go against the market? No one, I guess, that's when everyone enter the market and prices move like crazy in one direction. I recommend follow the trend, NEVER CHALLENGE the market, I learned from personal experience. So far, the system is working for me. If anyone noticed something different please let us know.   
We should be like bank traders, we should have our own trade rules that we must never violate!!!! avoid emotions, over trading, and forget about guts, that does not lead to success at least in trading. All my losses has come from guessing, overtrading, sticking to undisareable trades that last longer that expected, not recognizing a loss, that later becomes catasthrophic (both financially and emotional), not setting predefine rules with entry and exit points, stop-losses( not all trades will go as expected) and finally trying to reinvent the wheel(personally working and improving trading strategies, this forum is helping me). This market is rules set, we dont make the rules, big players make the rules at least in the short term, which is my trading strategy and for 99% of small stack traders. Who enter in a position for a year, a month, even a week, let say for an entire day, at least all my trades I generally close them in less than 30 minutes, some last days, small positions only, and with this system sometime after profit my 20 pips less than a minute. The market will finally correct after a combination of economic data and fundamentals, Banks or institutional investors has been here for centuries, and more to come profiting from unexperienced traders who enter the market dreaming to turn into the next Soros or Ihcan, and this guys are more sophisticated than any company out there. They have between others, but two major advantages: Technology(research-software) and Rules that make big players and any trading strategy succesful over the long run. I would include capital too $$$$, but biggest players have break down like LTCM, hegde funds like Amarath recently, and also banks who play against the market. Thanks to pablosky and others, we have some helpful tools, but what small investors also need are a set of unbreakable rules, like a trading bible that work according to a trader personality. I recommend to share your trading with a group of two, maximum three traders, It's definitely cost wise,funny, it has physical,mental,social, and healthy benefits, risk sharing, time saving, and force you to make the necessary rules to succeed in this difficult profession. Sometimes, the best system is not the most sophisticated and perfect, like the ones that Credit Suisse or Goldamn Sachs has, is the one that works for you personally and fit accordingly to your personality, eventhough has it flows and mistakes, everything needs readjustment, upgrades and constant changes until reach the desired perfection, also, the one that boost your confidence and finally make you successful. Good day and good Luck to all!!!! Thanks again for sharing your knowledge and research, I am trying and giving my best.

  * [#155](/thread/post/278356#post278356 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 21, 2007 2:24am  Apr 21, 2007 2:24am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar13263_4.gif) irusoh](irusoh)

  * | Joined Jul 2006  | Status: Stupid MQL Tricks Master | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=13263)

I don't know why so much fuss about repainting.  
Repainting is normal for many indicators. As price moves, conditions change and indicator repaints itself.  
Now, a real time testing is crucial because the way indicator looks on historical chart, is not necessarily how it happened in real life.  
For example if bar repaints itself from yellow to blue, it is good idea to exit short position, just what bluemiami did, I beleive. Sometimes 2 bars change from yellow to blue at once, thus real time entry is delayed since 2 bars that look blue on historical chart weren't blue when bar closed.  
The real time testing should be first accomplished with MT tester and then on demo account.

  * [#158](/thread/post/278654#post278654 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 21, 2007 2:25pm  Apr 21, 2007 2:25pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar17832_4.gif) TeamAphid](teamaphid)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: Team Work!!!! | [302 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=17832)

The backtests which will be done with repainting indicators are not reliable, as you all know. Therefore, only way is forward testing to understand if the system is profitable or not. The fuss for repainting indicators is about the time, because forward testing takes time.   
  
We asked our programmer about stepchoppy indicator and he said it can repaint after checking the codes for all four indicators. He says it repaints due to the StepRSI indicator which is used to calculate stepchoppy indicator. He said StepRSI calculates its values from the left of the chart, and not the right. Therefore at every new bar it recalculates everything, creating opportunity for repainting. He stated that the formulas "buffer" it very good, so it's not happening a lot but it can happen. This is the main reason you see it repaints more frequently on 15M chart than 4hr.  
  
We believe there are two ways to trade this system. One is after forward testing and observing the bars real time so that we can have more reliable test results. The other one is not to use stepchoppy indicator if you find it unreliable and use only ATR channels, Trend Power indicator and price action, all together. At the moment, we are forward testing pabloski system with our modified rules (we already backtested it with our modified rules, and the result has improved a lot but due to the repainting nature of stepchoppy indicator, we are not sure how this result is reliable), and we are also backtesting another modified pabloski system without using stephoppy indicator.  
  
We are going to share both systems here under pabloski thread to honour his generosity for sharing the indicators, his strategies and ideas.   
  
TeamAphid

[Please suggest a simple & effective Method/System of "Trading System" Forum to newbie](/thread/35860-please-suggest-a-simple-effective-methodsystem-of "Dear Friends in FF, 
  
I have read most threads of 5 stars trading strategys and methods form &quot;Trading System&quot; Forums of FF, but certain...") 180 replies

[The System Behind the System, by Merlin Jeffries](/thread/4446-the-system-behind-the-system-by-merlin-jeffries "Originally published in Stocks &amp; Commodities, February 2006 Issue. 
  
  
The System Behind The System 
by Merlin Jeffries, February 2006

  * [#161](/thread/post/278659#post278659 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 21, 2007 3:04pm  Apr 21, 2007 3:04pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar15327_5.gif) pabloski](pabloski)

  * | Joined Aug 2006  | Status: Trader | [356 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=15327) | Online Now 

> [Quoting TeamAphid](/thread/post/278654#post278654 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> The backtests which will be done with repainting indicators are not reliable, as you all know. Therefore, only way is forward testing to understand if the system is profitable or not. The fuss for repainting indicators is about the time, because forward testing takes time.   
>    
>  We asked our programmer about stepchoppy indicator and he said it can repaint after checking the codes for all four indicators. He says it repaints due to the StepRSI indicator which is used to calculate stepchoppy indicator. He said StepRSI calculates its values from the left of the chart, and not the right. Therefore at every new bar it recalculates everything, creating opportunity for repainting. He stated that the formulas "buffer" it very good, so it's not happening a lot but it can happen. This is the main reason you see it repaints more frequently on 15M chart than 4hr.  
>    
>  We believe there are two ways to trade this system. One is after forward testing and observing the bars real time so that we can have more reliable test results. The other one is not to use stepchoppy indicator if you find it unreliable and use only ATR channels, Trend Power indicator and price action, all together. At the moment, we are forward testing pabloski system with our modified rules (we already backtested it with our modified rules, and the result has improved a lot but due to the repainting nature of stepchoppy indicator, we are not sure how this result is reliable), and we are also backtesting another modified pabloski system without using stephoppy indicator.  
>    
>  We are going to share both systems here under pabloski thread to honour his generosity for sharing the indicators, his strategies and ideas.   
>    
>  TeamAphid
> 
> Ignored

TeamAphid, thank you for your continuous interest. Looking forward to cheking your variations!

  * | Joined Jul 2006  | Status: Stupid MQL Tricks Master | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=13263)

I like stepchoppy indicator, even though it repaints. I only saw it repaint one previous bar so far on 4hour chart. I couldn't find usefulness of trendpower indicator. Just from visual obsertvation it seemed to show all kinds of values on various system entries.  
But then again, as Team Aphid noted, I bastardized this system a lot in the course of my testing, so I don't know if I should post my results here in conflict with original.  
  
Among other things, I got rid of stoploss, i got rid of 2nd close, and I hold last unit until it goes opposite color or breaks the green line, just to name a few.   
It is still not perfect, there are a lot of things to be worked on, but I consider it a workable system to be put into forward test.

Hi Bluemiami!  
  
In terms of given signals, they are exactly the same. The first version of this indicator was StepChoppy. Then the author had the idea of showing the signals as candles or bars, so he created StepChoppyBars from StepChoppy v1.3.  
Both indicators will give the same signals (as they are actually the same indicator ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f633.png?v=15.1)) but in different ways, thats all! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

I have created an expert with quite different rules but nonetheless based on Pabloski's idea. I am now forward testing in and at the same time working on improvements.  
Entry/exit structure was greatly simplified. Also martingale like money management (I will call it smart martingale) was added to improve results.  
  
First buy was taken on NF on 2007.04.23 04:00 for 0.8 lots. It is now -84 pips.  
Additional buy was taken on 2007.04.24 04:46 for 0.8 lots. it is now +84.  
  
When I am satisfied with my system I will probably try to describe it in a separate thread.

  * [#187](/thread/post/281625#post281625 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 5:39pm  Apr 25, 2007 2:36pm | Edited 5:39pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar17832_4.gif) TeamAphid](teamaphid)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: Team Work!!!! | [302 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=17832)

Following rules are our modifications to pabloski system. They are only related to entry rules. We are going to explain modifications of SL and exit rules later.  
  
The main difference in entry compared to original pabloski is that we are not looking at the colour of previous bar to enter a trade as well as not waiting for a close between GREEN and AQUA ATR lines. Wherever the bar closes (up to 10 pips above AQUA ATR Line for longs and down to 10 pips below YELLOW ATR Line), if the bar colour changes to BLUE / RED, we see it as a strong indication of trend change and enter at close of that bar. Look at Jan 8th, 2007 12:00 bar entry instead of waiting for Jan 9th, 2007 08:00 bar original entry, 222 pips difference. Another example is on March 6th, 2007 00:00 bar, instead of original entry of March 8th, 2007 16:00 bar, 216 pips difference. Our backtest results show that this kind of entry improves the end result.  
  
Another main difference is that we are trading 4 lots instead of 3 to get better statistics and we did indeed.  
  
  
  
pabloski system entry rules modified by Team Aphid:  
  
Entry - Close above / below GREEN ATR line - NO ENTRY IF BAR CLOSES BELOW / ABOVE YELLOW / AQUA ATR LINE  
  
Special Condition 1 - If the close is 10 pips below / above YELLOW / AQUA ATR Line, then enter with 4 lots as if the price closes below / above AQUA / YELLOW ATR Line  
  
Special Condition 2 - If 4th lot exit is due to bar colour change (BLUE / RED), then reverse entry will be on the same bar (no need to wait for a close above / below GREEN ATR Line)  
  
Special Condition 3 - After exiting all 4 lots, you can reenter in the previous trade direction again if the bar colour triggers the trade(ie. You closed long position, after that if the bar colour turns to BLUE again and closes under AQUA ATR Line, then reenter with 4 lots to go long)

To summarize these rules:  
  
for buy:  
\- enter on close any time 2 last bars are red to blue.  
\- enter when close is between green line and aqua line + 10pips and previous close was below green line.  
\- enter when close between green line and aqua line + 10 pips and last bar was blue and close before that was above green line.  
  
Please, confirm.

I know you didn't ask me, but I think I understand it-  
  
BUY  
Blue bar closes **between** the green and aqua lines OR blue bar closes **above** the aqua line- the close being no more than 10 pips above the aqua line.  
  
SELL  
Red bar closes **between** the green and yellow lines OR  
red bar closes **below** the yellow line- the close being no more than 10 pips below the yellow line.

#  [](/thread/23592-pabloski-system)pabloski System 

  * 

  * [#201](/thread/post/1424924#post1424924 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 26, 2007 9:37am  Apr 26, 2007 9:37am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar17832_4.gif) TeamAphid](teamaphid)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: Team Work!!!! | [302 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=17832)

Let's say you exited all 4 lots and you have no position. Whenever you see a close with Blue bar and as long as the close is below aqua line +10 pips, enter long, no matter where the bar is. Even if the bar close is between red and orange ATR lines, if it is blue at close, enter long. If you see the blue bar appeared at close and above aqua line +10 pips, then NO entry. Our assumption is that blue bar shows a strong trend change, so NO NEED to wait until we have a close between green and aqua ATR lines. But if the close is above aqua + 10 pips, we assume we are late to catch the trend and we are not entering long.  
  
Look at the yellow arrow on folllowing chart. The blue bar is between orange and red, so this is a buy signal, no need to wait until a close between green and aqua lines.  
  
Therefore;  
  
BUY when BAR COLOUR IS BLUE and CLOSE IS ANYWHERE BELOW AQUA ATR LINE +10 PIPS  
  
Sorry for the confusion, we hope it is clear now.

Ahhhh, anyone reminded of a primary Vegas 4h tunnel signal? ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)  
I can see where Team Aphid got their idea from - stepchoppy turning blue is basically similiar to the 8 SMA changing the slope - there's been a change in trend, so we try to ride it as early as possible. Fake signals get compensated by the earlier entry.  
  
Nice idea and should really be better than waiting for a middle entry.  
  
This is also something I had wondered about in the high/low trending system of tkimble, who also uses a tunnel, but enters at the very outside boundary of it - the total opposite logic. You get guaranteed a late entry, because it tries to catch breakouts, but he tries to make up for it with a tiny stop.  
Here we try to get into changes early - sounds good to me, like I said, like the 4h Vegas tunnel logic.  
  
  
Not sure I've understood the SC 2 or the others yet, but that's most likely because I haven't put anything on my charts yet ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f61c.png?v=15.1)  
Sorry. Wanted to wait until all of the kinks are out and the super-optimized Team Aphid version is finalized ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)  
  
Btw, that screenshot above looks like a DBLHC or BUOB(the first blue bar with the arrow) =bullish reversal. Price action can also help along here ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)

Trust price. Know yourself.

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar14109_1.gif) SeekingLight](seekinglight)

  * Joined Jul 2006 | Status: Charts + PA > * | [3,251 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=14109)

Just threw it on a chart here.   
  
Currently looking over entries mostly. Checking whether a simple "turns to Red or Dark Blue, stop just below/above the bar" approach works out okay.  
  
Placing stops so far away manages to keep you in if the startup is choppy, but it can also wind up costly...would be the question whether one offsets the other.   
  
Also it seems better to do the TP on a touch of the ATR lines, not on a close?  
Each blue hue being a quarter, the last quarter kept until we move back more than 2 ATR lines or color changes for example...  
  
I'm also wondering about entering again after lighter hue blues turn dark again..same for the reds.  
This might be what Team Aphid means with one of their special rules?  
I may have simply missed some stuff, I'm sorry, I'm trading alongside as I write this and cable just completely lost it, so 80% attention is somewhere else ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f61c.png?v=15.1)

Trust price. Know yourself.

  * [#210](/thread/post/1425567#post1425567 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 26, 2007 10:48pm  Apr 26, 2007 10:48pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar17832_4.gif) TeamAphid](teamaphid)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: Team Work!!!! | [302 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=17832)

Hi all,  
  
As you know we are trying to improve pabloski system further. But today something important happened. As aktaurus indicated a few times, stepchoppy indicator is repainting and we believe our backtest results or anyone's backtest results cannot be correct.   
  
Please have a look at following two charts, and especially the last two bars. They are the same charts and saved within 10 minutes respectively. We were holding our short position @ 236.33 until today but a few hours ago, when GBPJPY started to climb, then current bar (08:00 bar) (now 12:00 bar is current) and previous bar (04:00 bar) were both yellow first, when the price passes 238.40 level, all of a sudden, last two bars became blue. Then when price retraced back towards 238 level, they became yellow again. If the price had climbed further and closed at let's say 238.70, the last two bars would have stayed as blue and according to original rules and our modified rules, we should have exited at close of 04.00 bar at 237.96 which was impossible at that time.   
  
We know trades are taken at the close of the bar, but since it also repaints previous bar, it is even impossible to forward test this system. Therefore, as Team Aphid, we are not going to use stepchoppy indicator in our modifications. Therefore, please discard our previous post explaining our modified entries.   
  
We said we are also working on another version of pabloski system which is not using stepchoppy indicator. It is still work in progress and whenever we finish it, if we satisfy with the test results, we are going to explain its rules in this thread again.  
  
Once again, stepchoppy indicator is unstable and cannot be backtested and forward tested properly and cannot be traded either. 

Attached Images

![](/attachment/image/29672?d=1177590744) ![](/attachment/image/29673?d=1177590744)

That is why visual backtesting on MT backtester is very reliable. It shows in real time what is happeneing.  
I ran special stats on backtester and found that at the close of the bar there is never previous bar yellow, and that is they both turn blue at the same time so you are looking back at 2 blue bars.  
  
Anyway, here is my basic stepchoppy strategy, which you are welcome to test and comment on:  
  
It's very simple.  
Buy: on 4hour open when last bar is blue and 2nd bar is blue or dodgerblue or red.  
close buy on 4hour open when last bar is red, orange, tomato or yellow (its' not of blue colors).  
Sell: on 4hour open when last bar is red and 2nd bar is red or aqua or blue.  
close buy on 4hour open when last bar is blue, dodgerblue, lightblue or aqua (its' not of red colors).  
  
I don't use ATR channels at all.  
Oh, I adjusted kv=0.8, it seemed to work a little better.  
Here are some results of backtest with pabloski original system, and my system with variations using money management.

  * [#214](/thread/post/1425793#post1425793 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 27, 2007 2:24am  Apr 27, 2007 2:24am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar13263_4.gif) irusoh](irusoh)

  * | Joined Jul 2006  | Status: Stupid MQL Tricks Master | [288 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=13263)

> [Quoting billbss](/thread/post/1425763#post1425763 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> What is your progressive money management?  
>    
>  Thanks
> 
> Ignored

Basically I increase a size incementally say by 10-20% as i lose, so first loss is 1 lot, 2nd 1.2 lot, 3rd 1.4 and so on. You lose when price is ranging. Usually after 3-5 losses comes a big run so I get it all back and more.  
If you look at results, flat MM increased original size no more than 4-5 times and progressive about 10-12 times.  
With progressive after so many losses, say 4 or 5, I start increasing size in larger chunks instead of 0.2 by 0.4. Logic is the big run must be close.  
So let's say you lose 4 times, each time you add 0.2, now your size is 1.8  
on 5th time and forward you increase double so 1original + 5losses * 0.4 double increment = 3 lots next bet.  
I also decrease loss count by 2 every time I win.  
  
This is a rough cut, it could be refined, but it should work with winning strategy like this improving your results.

> That is why visual backtesting on MT backtester is very reliable. It shows in real time what is happeneing.  
>  I ran special stats on backtester and found that at the close of the bar there is never previous bar yellow, and that is they both turn blue at the same time so you are looking back at 2 blue bars.  
>    
>  Anyway, here is my basic stepchoppy strategy, which you are welcome to test and comment on:  
>    
>  It's very simple.  
>  Buy: on 4hour open when last bar is blue and 2nd bar is blue or dodgerblue or red.  
>  close buy on 4hour open when last bar is red, orange, tomato or yellow (its' not of blue colors).  
>  Sell: on 4hour open when last bar is red and 2nd bar is red or aqua or blue.  
>  close buy on 4hour open when last bar is blue, dodgerblue, lightblue or aqua (its' not of red colors).  
>    
>  I don't use ATR channels at all.  
>  Oh, I adjusted kv=0.8, it seemed to work a little better.  
>  Here are some results of backtest with pabloski original system, and my system with variations using money management.

Hi everyone,  
  
After "igorad" fixed repainting issue of stepchoppy indicator, we started working on pabloski again and we did many backtests last week. And we believe we now have a tradable version of pabloski with much lower drawdowns and better risk reward ratio.  
  
We are going to explain all details of our modified version of pabloski system and also send alerts for a while as soon as a signal is triggered so that you can walk with us to learn this system.   
  
Before we start explaining the system, first you need a correct setup of GBPJPY chart with required indicators.  
  
Use GBPJPY 4hr chart.  
  
You'll need all indicators attached on post # 2 by pabloski (this set of indicators includes repainting stepchoppy indi and we are going to use that one together with igorad's NOT repainting stepchoppy indi).  
  
You need to attach Trend Power indicator to your chart as well (go to post #162).  
  
You'll also need to attach NOT repainting version of Stepchoppy indicator (go to post #219).  
  
As a result of above attachments, your chart should look like as follows:

#  [](/thread/23592-pabloski-system)pabloski System 

  * 

  * [#241](/thread/post/1433315#post1433315 "Post Permalink")

  * May 5, 2007 5:56pm  May 5, 2007 5:56pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar17832_4.gif) TeamAphid](teamaphid)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: Team Work!!!! | [302 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=17832)

ENTRY RULES:  
  
1- For long trades, look at bar colours of stepchoppy (SC) indicators. If they are both blue AND they are below AQUA ATR Line + 10 pips (anywhere below it, NOT ONLY between GREEN and AQUA ATR Lines), then enter at the close or immediately at the open of next bar with 4 lots. Following charts show two examples of correct Long entries.  
  
Look at vertical white line and the close of the bars. Both pictures show that repainting (on the chart) and NOT repainting (the bottom window) versions of SC indicator changed the bar colour to BLUE at the same time, on the same bar (see assumption below). The place of bars is not important, in the first picture close of the bar is between GREEN and YELLOW ATR Lines. In the second picture, it is between ORANGE and RED ATR Lines.  
  
So we enter long with 4 lots at the close these bars or opening of the next bar by assuming downtrend ended and uptrend started because of BLUE bars.  
  
Another assumption here during backtesting was repainting version on the chart repainted previous bar to LIGHT BLUE (14/3/2007 08:00 bar) at the end of the BLUE line (14/3/2007 12:00 bar) in the first picture and corresponding bar in the second picture so that we had BLUE bars on both versions of the SC indicator. If this assumption is not true in real time, then we'll use another entry method which will be explained in the next post. 

Attached Images

![](/attachment/image/30657?d=1178353880) ![](/attachment/image/30658?d=1178353880)

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#242](/thread/post/1433323#post1433323 "Post Permalink")

  * May 5, 2007 6:38pm  May 5, 2007 6:38pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar17832_4.gif) TeamAphid](teamaphid)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: Team Work!!!! | [302 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=17832)

ENTRY RULES:  
  
2- Most of the time, BLUE bar on repainting version will not match the BLUE bar on NOT repainting version. Before we had NOT repainting version, we did backtests with repainting one and results were more than satisfactory. Therefore, if we can enter at the same level by using NOT repainting version, then we can duplicate those results. So, we have decided to enter a limit order at the close of the first BLUE bar of NOT repainting version by using the close of the first BLUE bar of repainting version.  
  
Have a look at the following chart. BLUE bars do not match, so when the price closed at 231.72, repainting version repainted the previous bar to BLUE, so we should have entered at 231.52, but we are one bar ahead now. Therefore, enter a limit BUY order at 231.52 with 4 lots when the price is at 231.72 and wait for your limit order to be filled. Your limit order was filled on 30/3/2007 00:00 bar at 231.52.  
  
What happens if price does not hit that limit entry level? Are we going to miss the trade? Of course not, please see next post for that.  
  
ps. we are using alpari ru. server for all our illustrations. 

Attached Image

![](/attachment/image/30664?d=1178357883)

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#243](/thread/post/1433342#post1433342 "Post Permalink")

  * May 5, 2007 8:10pm  May 5, 2007 8:10pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar17832_4.gif) TeamAphid](teamaphid)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: Team Work!!!! | [302 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=17832)

ENTRY RULES:  
  
3- Please have a look at the first chart. According to rule #2, we should put our buy limit order at 234.05 (close of 20/2/2007 08:00 bar) at the close of 12:00 bar. But look at the vertical white line (12:00 bar) where the value of Trend Power indicator is 0.14 at the close. In this case, we are not going to put a buy limit order at 234.05 and we will open a long position with 4 lots at 234.97 (close of 12:00 bar). So, before putting a limit buy order, you should look at the value of Trend Power indicator, if it is equal to or greater than 0.14, then you will buy at the close of the bar or open of the next bar, no need to put a limit order. In this example, the value of Trend Power indicator became 0.14 when NOT painting SC turned to BLUE.   
  
There are some cases it turns to BLUE a few bars later (look at the second chart). In that case, first put a limit buy order at the price of first BLUE bar of repainting SC and then watch Trend Power indicator. If your limit order is filled, then you are in position and no problem. If the price does not hit your limit order, then cancel your limit order and open a position at the close of the bar WHEN the value of Trend Power indicator is 0.14 or greater. 

Attached Images

Couple of questions, just to make sure,  
  
Must the previous non-repainting bar always be blue for a limit order entry?  
  
Must it be always blue for a TrendPower entry?  
  
With either a TrendPower entry or a limit order entry, must we still observe the Aqua+10 pips limitation?

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#246](/thread/post/1433611#post1433611 "Post Permalink")

  * May 6, 2007 10:19am  May 6, 2007 10:19am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar17832_4.gif) TeamAphid](teamaphid)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: Team Work!!!! | [302 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=17832)

We are not interested in the colour of previous non-repainting bar. But we are looking at it on repainting SC.  
  
For TrendPower entry, both non-repainting and repainting bars should be blue AND previous repainting bar should be blue as well. If not, since they are both blue, you will enter without checking TrendPower indicator - Entry Rule #1  
  
Yes, you will observe Aqua +10 pips limitation all the time.  
  
Btw, your assumption of shorts being just the opposite- red bars and a -.14 Trend Power reading is correct.  
  
But we have an observation here, red bars on repainting and non-repainting SC match all the time. Therefore, whenever you see a red bar on non-repainting SC, if it is above yellow -10 pips limitation, then you can go short.

TeamAphid, thanks for all your hard work and back/forward testing and development of this method!  
  
It seems that these news rules add a certain level of complexity to the system. Have you considered simply using the new non-repainting indicator the same as we used the repainting indicator before? Could the loss in pips due to entering one or two bars later be that much?   * [#248](/thread/post/1433672#post1433672 "Post Permalink")

  * May 6, 2007 4:19pm  May 6, 2007 4:19pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar35717_6.gif) JoshDance](joshdance)

  * | Joined Mar 2007  | Status: Trader | [606 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=35717)

I've taken the newest entry criteria from TeamAphid and consolidated it into the following... TeamAphid, please check these for validity:  
  
==============================================  
SCv1 = Repainting version of indicator (the one on the price)  
SCv2 = Non-repainting version of indicator (the one in the separate window)  
  
Long entry:  
  
In all cases, the previous bar close must be below the aqua line + 10 pips.  
  
Wait for a blue bar on SCv2.  
  
(1) If the corresponding bar on SCv1 is the first blue bar, or if the TrendPower indicator is >= 0.14, (or both, obviously), enter long now. Entry is done.  
  
(2) Else, if there are prior blue bars on SCv1 and the TrendPower indicator is < 0.14, place a buy limit order at the closing price of the first blue bar on SCv1.  
  
Check the charts at the next bar close.  
- If this closed bar caused the buy limit order to get filled, our entry is done.  
- If the buy limit is still open, and if TrendPower is >= 0.14, enter long (and obviously, cancel the buy limit order)—entry done. Else, wait until next bar close and recheck.  
  
Obviously, if a non-blue-shaded bar appears, we abort our entry.  
================================================ 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#249](/thread/post/1434087#post1434087 "Post Permalink")

  * May 7, 2007 10:46am  May 7, 2007 10:46am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar17832_4.gif) TeamAphid](teamaphid)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: Team Work!!!! | [302 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=17832)

We have considered simply using the new non-repainting indicator the same as we used the repainting indicator before and we already backtested it. The reason why we were trying to match the previous indicator's entries is that there was approximately 6,000 pips difference in 15 months of backtesting period if we could have entered with repainting indicator's signal. But instead of using our 3 entry rules (limit orders, trend power entry etc.), if you use the new non-repainting indicator for entry (BUY when the bar is blue AND the close is below aqua atr +10 or vice versa), you will get 465 pips less compared to our entry rules, it is not actually a big deal.   
  
Therefore, for the sake of simplicity, we agree with you using just non-repainting SC blue and red bars for entries.  
  
We'll post SL and exit rules asap.  
  
Thanks for your contribution.  
  
  
  

> [Quoting JoshDance](/thread/post/1433665#post1433665 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> TeamAphid, thanks for all your hard work and back/forward testing and development of this method!  
>    
>  It seems that these news rules add a certain level of complexity to the system. Have you considered simply using the new non-repainting indicator the same as we used the repainting indicator before? Could the loss in pips due to entering one or two bars later be that much? In your last post in this chart ( [http://www.forexfactory.com/attachme...9&d=1178363236](http://www.forexfactory.com/attachment.php?attachmentid=30669&d=1178363236) ), we missed over 100 pips because we waited for the price to retrace to the previous bar's close, and if we had just placed our long order when the non-repainting indicator bar turned blue, then we would have made many more pips.  
>    
>  It just seems that trying to get this to match the previous indicator's entries is a long way around what should be a shorter path. Am I missing something, or do I not understand, or...?  
>    
>  Also, looking forward to SL and exit rules!
